<p>The <b>Kansas City Chiefs</b> are a professional <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American football</a> team based in <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City,_Missouri" title="Kansas City, Missouri">Kansas City, Missouri</a>. The Chiefs compete in the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a> (NFL) as a member club of the league's <a href="/wiki/American_Football_Conference" title="American Football Conference">American Football Conference</a> (AFC) <a href="/wiki/AFC_West" title="AFC West">West</a> division. The team was founded in 1960 as the <b>Dallas Texans</b> by businessman <a href="/wiki/Lamar_Hunt" title="Lamar Hunt">Lamar Hunt</a> and was a charter member of the <a href="/wiki/American_Football_League" title="American Football League">American Football League</a> (AFL). (It is not associated with the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">NFL</a> <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Texans_(NFL)" title="Dallas Texans (NFL)">Dallas Texans</a>.) In 1963, the team <a href="/wiki/Relocation_of_professional_sports_teams" title="Relocation of professional sports teams">moved</a> to Kansas City and assumed its current name.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The Chiefs joined the NFL as a result of the <a href="/wiki/AFL%E2%80%93NFL_merger" title="AFL–NFL merger">merger</a> in 1970. The team is valued at over $2 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-Forbes_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forbes-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Hunt's son, <a href="/wiki/Clark_Hunt" title="Clark Hunt">Clark</a>, serves as chairman and CEO. While Hunt's ownership stakes passed collectively to his widow and children after his death in 2006, Clark is the operating head of the franchise; he represents the Chiefs at all league meetings and has ultimate authority on personnel changes.
</p><p>The Chiefs have won three AFL championships, in 1962, 1966, and 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-PFHOF_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFHOF-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> They became the second AFL team (after the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Jets" title="New York Jets">New York Jets</a>) to defeat an NFL team in an <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">AFL–NFL World Championship Game</a>, when they defeated the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Vikings" title="Minnesota Vikings">Minnesota Vikings</a> in <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_IV" title="Super Bowl IV">Super Bowl IV</a>. The team's victory on January 11, 1970, was the final such competition before the leagues' merger went into full effect. The Chiefs were also the second team, after the <a href="/wiki/Green_Bay_Packers" title="Green Bay Packers">Green Bay Packers</a>, to appear in more than one Super Bowl (and the first AFL team to do so) and the first to appear in the championship game in two different decades. Despite post-season success early in the franchise's history, winning five of their first six postseason games, the team struggled to find success in the playoffs for many years, including losing 10 of 11 playoff games from 1993 to 2017, which included an 8-game losing streak. Since then, the Chiefs have won 4 of their last 5 playoff games, including <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_LIV" title="Super Bowl LIV">Super Bowl LIV</a> in 2020, which earned the franchise their first championship in 50 years.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Franchise_history">Franchise history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kansas_City_Chiefs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Franchise history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Kansas_City_Chiefs" title="History of the Kansas City Chiefs">History of the Kansas City Chiefs</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Formation">Formation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kansas_City_Chiefs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Formation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1959, <a href="/wiki/Lamar_Hunt" title="Lamar Hunt">Lamar Hunt</a> began discussions with other businessmen to establish a professional football league that would rival the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PFHOF_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFHOF-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AFL_Origins_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFL_Origins-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Hunt's desire to secure a football team was heightened after watching the <a href="/wiki/1958_NFL_Championship_Game" title="1958 NFL Championship Game">1958 NFL Championship Game</a> between the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Giants" title="New York Giants">New York Giants</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Colts" class="mw-redirect" title="Baltimore Colts">Baltimore Colts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AFL_Origins_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFL_Origins-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Althaus_35_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Althaus_35-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> After unsuccessful attempts to purchase and relocate the NFL's <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cardinals_(NFL,_1920%E2%80%9359)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chicago Cardinals (NFL, 1920–59)">Chicago Cardinals</a> to his hometown of <a href="/wiki/Dallas,_Texas" class="mw-redirect" title="Dallas, Texas">Dallas, Texas</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-PFHOF_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFHOF-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-History_60s_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_60s-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Hunt went to the NFL and asked to create an expansion franchise in Dallas. The NFL turned him down, so Hunt then established the <a href="/wiki/American_Football_League" title="American Football League">American Football League</a> and started his own team, the Dallas Texans, to begin play in 1960. Hunt hired a little-known assistant coach from the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Hurricanes_football" title="Miami Hurricanes football">University of Miami football team</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hank_Stram" title="Hank Stram">Hank Stram</a>, to be the team's head coach<sup id="cite_ref-AFL_Origins_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFL_Origins-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> after the job offer was declined by <a href="/wiki/Bud_Wilkinson" title="Bud Wilkinson">Bud Wilkinson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tom_Landry" title="Tom Landry">Tom Landry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AFL_Origins_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFL_Origins-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After Stram was hired, Don Klosterman was hired as head scout, credited by many for bringing a wealth of talent to the Texans after luring it away from the NFL, often hiding players and using creative means to land them.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kansas_City_Chiefs_at_Denver_Broncos_1985-12-14_(ticket)_(crop).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Kansas_City_Chiefs_at_Denver_Broncos_1985-12-14_%28ticket%29_%28crop%29.jpg/200px-Kansas_City_Chiefs_at_Denver_Broncos_1985-12-14_%28ticket%29_%28crop%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Kansas_City_Chiefs_at_Denver_Broncos_1985-12-14_%28ticket%29_%28crop%29.jpg/300px-Kansas_City_Chiefs_at_Denver_Broncos_1985-12-14_%28ticket%29_%28crop%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/84/Kansas_City_Chiefs_at_Denver_Broncos_1985-12-14_%28ticket%29_%28crop%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="314" data-file-height="272" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kansas_City_Chiefs_at_Denver_Broncos_1985-12-14_(ticket)_(crop).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Len_Dawson" title="Len Dawson">Len Dawson</a> led the Chiefs to victory in <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_IV" title="Super Bowl IV">Super Bowl IV</a> and was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Pro_Football_Hall_of_Fame" title="Pro Football Hall of Fame">Pro Football Hall of Fame</a> in 1987</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_success">Early success</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kansas_City_Chiefs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early success">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Texans shared the <a href="/wiki/Cotton_Bowl_(stadium)" title="Cotton Bowl (stadium)">Cotton Bowl</a> with the NFL's cross-town competition <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Cowboys" title="Dallas Cowboys">Dallas Cowboys</a> for three seasons. The Texans were to have exclusive access to the stadium until the NFL put an expansion team, the Dallas Cowboys, there.<sup id="cite_ref-AFL_Origins_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFL_Origins-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> While the team averaged a league-best 24,500 at the Cotton Bowl, the Texans gained less attention due to the AFL's relatively lower profile compared to the NFL.<sup id="cite_ref-AFL_Origins_9-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFL_Origins-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> In the franchise's first two seasons, the team managed only an 8–6 and 6–8 record, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-PFR_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFR-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In their third season, the Texans strolled to an 11–3 record and a berth in the team's first <a href="/wiki/American_Football_League_playoffs" title="American Football League playoffs">American Football League Championship Game</a>, against the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Oilers" class="mw-redirect" title="Houston Oilers">Houston Oilers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-History_60s_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_60s-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PFR_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFR-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The game was broadcast nationally on <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a> and the Texans defeated the Oilers 20–17 in double overtime.<sup id="cite_ref-History_60s_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_60s-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The game lasted 77 minutes and 54 seconds, which still stands as the longest championship game in professional football history.<sup id="cite_ref-History_60s_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_60s-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It turned out to be the last game the team would play as the Dallas Texans. Despite competing against a Cowboys team that managed only a 9–28–3 record in their first three seasons, Hunt decided that the <a href="/wiki/Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_Metroplex" class="mw-redirect" title="Dallas–Fort Worth Metroplex">Dallas–Fort Worth</a> <a href="/wiki/Media_market" title="Media market">media market</a> could not sustain two professional football franchises.<sup id="cite_ref-History_60s_12-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_60s-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-This_Week_February_8,_2008_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-This_Week_February_8,_2008-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> He considered moving the Texans to either <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a> or <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a> for the 1963 season.<sup id="cite_ref-History_60s_12-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_60s-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> However, he was ultimately swayed by an offer from <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City,_Missouri" title="Kansas City, Missouri">Kansas City</a> Mayor <a href="/wiki/Harold_Roe_Bartle" title="Harold Roe Bartle">Harold Roe Bartle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-History_60s_12-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_60s-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-This_Week_February_8,_2008_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-This_Week_February_8,_2008-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gruver_103_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gruver_103-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Bartle promised to triple the franchise's season ticket sales and expand the seating capacity of <a href="/wiki/Municipal_Stadium_(Kansas_City,_Missouri)" title="Municipal Stadium (Kansas City, Missouri)">Municipal Stadium</a> to accommodate the team.<sup id="cite_ref-History_60s_12-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_60s-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-This_Week_February_8,_2008_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-This_Week_February_8,_2008-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gruver_103_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gruver_103-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hunt agreed to <a href="/wiki/Relocation_of_professional_sports_teams" title="Relocation of professional sports teams">relocate</a> the franchise to Kansas City on May 22, 1963, and on May 26 the team was renamed the Kansas City Chiefs.<sup id="cite_ref-History_60s_12-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_60s-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-This_Week_February_8,_2008_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-This_Week_February_8,_2008-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gruver_103_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gruver_103-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Hunt and head coach Hank Stram initially planned to retain the Texans name, but a fan contest determined the new "Chiefs" name in honor of Mayor Bartle's nickname that he acquired in his professional role as Scout Executive of the St. Joseph and Kansas City Boy Scout Councils and founder of the Scouting Society, the <a href="/wiki/Tribe_of_Mic-O-Say" title="Tribe of Mic-O-Say">Tribe of Mic-O-Say</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-History_60s_12-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_60s-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gruver_103_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gruver_103-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The franchise became one of the strongest teams in the now thriving American Football League,<sup id="cite_ref-PFHOF_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFHOF-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> with the most playoff appearances for an AFL team (tied with the <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Raiders" class="mw-redirect" title="Oakland Raiders">Oakland Raiders</a>), and the most AFL Championships (3).<sup id="cite_ref-History_60s_12-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_60s-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The team's dominance helped Lamar Hunt become a central figure in negotiations with NFL Commissioner <a href="/wiki/Pete_Rozelle" title="Pete Rozelle">Pete Rozelle</a> to agree on an <a href="/wiki/AFL%E2%80%93NFL_merger" title="AFL–NFL merger">AFL–NFL merger</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-History_60s_12-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_60s-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Maske,_Mark_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maske,_Mark-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> In the meetings between the two leagues, a <a href="/wiki/Professional_American_football_championship_games" title="Professional American football championship games">merged league championship game</a> was agreed to be played in January 1967 following the conclusion of the leagues' respective 1966 seasons. Hunt insisted on calling the game the "Super Bowl" after seeing his children playing with a popular toy at the time, a <a href="/wiki/Super_Ball" title="Super Ball">Super Ball</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-History_60s_12-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_60s-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Maske,_Mark_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maske,_Mark-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> While the first few games were designated the "AFL–NFL World Championship Game", the Super Bowl name became its officially licensed title in years to come.
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r923042769/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:left;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption-center{text-align:center;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti
