.trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:288px;max-width:288px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:142px;max-width:142px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:1986_Jeno%27s_Pizza_-_49_-_Robert_Holmes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/1986_Jeno%27s_Pizza_-_49_-_Robert_Holmes.jpg/140px-1986_Jeno%27s_Pizza_-_49_-_Robert_Holmes.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" height="196" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b3/1986_Jeno%27s_Pizza_-_49_-_Robert_Holmes.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="143" data-file-height="200" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:142px;max-width:142px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:1986_Jeno%27s_Pizza_-_50_-_Buck_Buchanan_and_Curley_Culp.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/1986_Jeno%27s_Pizza_-_50_-_Buck_Buchanan_and_Curley_Culp.jpg/140px-1986_Jeno%27s_Pizza_-_50_-_Buck_Buchanan_and_Curley_Culp.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" height="196" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b5/1986_Jeno%27s_Pizza_-_50_-_Buck_Buchanan_and_Curley_Culp.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="143" data-file-height="200" /></a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="thumbcaption" style="background-color:transparent">The Chiefs topped the Raiders in the <a href="/wiki/1969_American_Football_League_Championship_Game" title="1969 American Football League Championship Game">1969 AFL championship game</a> (<i>left</i>) and went on to defeat the Vikings in Super Bowl IV (<i>right</i>)</div></div></div></div>
<p>The Chiefs cruised to an 11–2–1 record in 1966, and defeated the defending AFL Champion <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Bills" title="Buffalo Bills">Buffalo Bills</a> in the AFL Championship Game.<sup id="cite_ref-Gruver_167_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gruver_167-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The Chiefs were invited to play the NFL's league champion <a href="/wiki/Green_Bay_Packers" title="Green Bay Packers">Green Bay Packers</a> in <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_I" title="Super Bowl I">the first AFL–NFL World Championship Game</a>. Kansas City and Green Bay played a close game for the first half, but Green Bay took control in the final two quarters, winning the game by a score of 35–10.<sup id="cite_ref-History_60s_12-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_60s-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The Chiefs lost the game but gained the respect of several Packers opponents following the game.<sup id="cite_ref-Gruver_179_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gruver_179-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The Chiefs' inter-league match-up with the Packers was not the last time that they would face an NFL opponent, especially on the championship stage.<sup id="cite_ref-History_60s_12-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_60s-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The following August, Kansas City hosted the NFL's <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Bears" title="Chicago Bears">Chicago Bears</a> in the 1967 preseason and won the game 66–24.<sup id="cite_ref-History_60s_12-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_60s-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite losing to the division rival Oakland Raiders twice in the regular season in 1969, the two teams met for a third time in the AFL Championship Game where Kansas City won 17–7.<sup id="cite_ref-PFR_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFR-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Backup quarterback <a href="/wiki/Mike_Livingston" title="Mike Livingston">Mike Livingston</a> led the team in a six-game winning streak after <a href="/wiki/Len_Dawson" title="Len Dawson">Len Dawson</a> suffered a leg injury which kept him out of most of the season's games.<sup id="cite_ref-History_60s_12-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_60s-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> While getting plenty of help from the club's defense, Dawson returned from the injury and led the Chiefs to <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_IV" title="Super Bowl IV">Super Bowl IV</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-History_60s_12-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_60s-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Against the NFL champion <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Vikings" title="Minnesota Vikings">Minnesota Vikings</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-PFHOF_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFHOF-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> who were <a href="/wiki/Spread_betting" title="Spread betting">favored</a> by 12½, the Chiefs dominated the game 23–7 to claim the team's first Super Bowl championship.<sup id="cite_ref-History_60s_12-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_60s-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Dawson was named the game's <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="Super Bowl Most Valuable Player Award">Most Valuable Player</a> after completing 12-of-17 passes for 142 yards and one touchdown, with 1 interception.<sup id="cite_ref-Dawson_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dawson-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The following season, the Chiefs and the rest of the American Football League merged with the National Football League after the AFL–NFL merger became official.<sup id="cite_ref-History_60s_12-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_60s-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The Chiefs were placed in the <a href="/wiki/American_Football_Conference" title="American Football Conference">American Football Conference</a>'s <a href="/wiki/American_Football_Conference_West_Division" class="mw-redirect" title="American Football Conference West Division">West Division</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PFR_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFR-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From 1960 to 1969, the Chiefs/Texans won 87 games, which is the most in the 10-year history of the AFL.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1970, the Chiefs won only seven games in their first season in the NFL and missed the playoffs.<sup id="cite_ref-PFR_13-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFR-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The following season, the Chiefs tallied a 10–3–1 record and won the AFC West Division.<sup id="cite_ref-History_70s_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_70s-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Head coach Hank Stram considered his 1971 Chiefs team as his best, but they failed to capture their championship dominance from 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-History_70s_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_70s-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Most of the pieces of the team which won Super Bowl IV two years earlier were still in place for the 1971 season.<sup id="cite_ref-History_70s_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_70s-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The Chiefs tied with the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Dolphins" title="Miami Dolphins">Miami Dolphins</a> for the best record in the AFC, and both teams met in a <a href="/wiki/Christmas_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Christmas Day">Christmas Day</a> playoff game which the Chiefs lost 27–24 in double overtime.<sup id="cite_ref-History_70s_22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_70s-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The Dolphins outlasted the Chiefs with a 37-yard <a href="/wiki/Field_goal_(football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Field goal (football)">field goal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-History_70s_22-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_70s-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The game surpassed the 1962 AFL Championship Game as the longest ever at 82 minutes and 40 seconds.<sup id="cite_ref-History_70s_22-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_70s-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The game was also the final football game at Kansas City's Municipal Stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-History_70s_22-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_70s-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1972, the Chiefs moved into the newly constructed <a href="/wiki/Arrowhead_Stadium" title="Arrowhead Stadium">Arrowhead Stadium</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Truman_Sports_Complex" title="Truman Sports Complex">Truman Sports Complex</a> outside of <a href="/wiki/CBD-Downtown,_Kansas_City" class="mw-redirect" title="CBD-Downtown, Kansas City">Downtown Kansas City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-History_70s_22-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_70s-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The team's first game at Arrowhead was against the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals_(NFL)" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Louis Cardinals (NFL)">St. Louis Cardinals</a>, a preseason game which the Chiefs won 24–14.<sup id="cite_ref-History_70s_22-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_70s-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Linebacker <a href="/wiki/Willie_Lanier" title="Willie Lanier">Willie Lanier</a> and quarterback Len Dawson won the <a href="/wiki/Walter_Payton_Man_of_the_Year_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Walter Payton Man of the Year Award">NFL Man of the Year Award</a> in 1972 and 1973, respectively.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Decline">Decline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kansas_City_Chiefs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Decline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Chiefs would not return to the <a href="/wiki/NFL_playoffs" title="NFL playoffs">post-season</a> for the remainder of the 1970s, and the 1973 season was the team's last winning effort for seven years.<sup id="cite_ref-History_70s_22-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_70s-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Hank Stram was fired following a 5–9 season in 1974, and many of the Chiefs' future <a href="/wiki/Pro_Football_Hall_of_Fame" title="Pro Football Hall of Fame">Hall of Fame</a> players would depart by the middle of the decade.<sup id="cite_ref-History_70s_22-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_70s-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> From 1975 to 1988, the Chiefs had become a team that rarely won which provided Chiefs fans with nothing but futility.<sup id="cite_ref-Althaus_97_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Althaus_97-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Althaus_101_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Althaus_101-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Five head coaches struggled to achieve the same success as Stram, compiling an 81–121–1 record.<sup id="cite_ref-Althaus_97_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Althaus_97-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1980, Coach Marv Levy cut future Hall of Fame Kicker <a href="/wiki/Jan_Stenerud" title="Jan Stenerud">Jan Stenerud</a> for little known <a href="/wiki/Nick_Lowery" title="Nick Lowery">Nick Lowery</a>, who would become the most accurate kicker in NFL History over the next 14 years. In 1981, running back <a href="/wiki/Joe_Delaney" title="Joe Delaney">Joe Delaney</a> rushed for 1,121 yards and was named the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League_Rookie_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="National Football League Rookie of the Year">AFC Rookie of the Year</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-History_80s_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_80s-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The Chiefs finished the season with a 9–7 record and entered the 1982 season with optimism.<sup id="cite_ref-History_80s_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_80s-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> However, the <a href="/wiki/1982_NFL_strike" class="mw-redirect" title="1982 NFL strike">NFL Players Association strike</a> curbed the Chiefs' chances of returning to the postseason for the first time in over a decade.<sup id="cite_ref-History_80s_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_80s-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The Chiefs tallied a 3–6 record<sup id="cite_ref-PFR_13-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFR-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> and in the off-season, Joe Delaney died while trying to save several children from drowning in a pond near his home in Louisiana.<sup id="cite_ref-Joe_Delaney_headed_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Joe_Delaney_headed-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Chiefs made a mistake in drafting quarterback <a href="/wiki/Todd_Blackledge" title="Todd Blackledge">Todd Blackledge</a> over future greats such as <a href="/wiki/Jim_Kelly" title="Jim Kelly">Jim Kelly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dan_Marino" title="Dan Marino">Dan Marino</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1983_NFL_Draft" title="1983 NFL Draft">1983 NFL Draft</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Althaus_167_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Althaus_167-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Warrick_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Warrick-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Blackledge never started a full season for Kansas City while Kelly and Marino played Hall of Fame careers.<sup id="cite_ref-Warrick_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Warrick-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> While the Chiefs struggled on offense in the 1980s, the Chiefs had a strong defensive unit consisting of Pro Bowlers such as <a href="/wiki/Bill_Maas" title="Bill Maas">Bill Maas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Lewis_(American_football)" title="Albert Lewis (American football)">Albert Lewis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Art_Still" title="Art Still">Art Still</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deron_Cherry" title="Deron Cherry">Deron Cherry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-History_80s_25-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_80s-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/John_Mackovic" title="John Mackovic">John Mackovic</a> took over head coaching duties for the 1983 season after <a href="/wiki/Marv_Levy" title="Marv Levy">Marv Levy</a> was fired.<sup id="cite_ref-History_80s_25-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_80s-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Over the next four seasons, Mackovic coached the Chiefs to a 30–34 record, but took the team to its first post-season appearance in 15 years in the <a href="/wiki/NFL_playoffs,_1986%E2%80%9387" class="mw-redirect" title="NFL playoffs, 1986–87">1986 NFL playoffs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PFR_13-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFR-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> They lost to the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Jets" title="New York Jets">New York Jets</a> in the wild-card round.<sup id="cite_ref-History_80s_25-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_80s-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Despite leading the Chiefs to only their third winning season and second playoff appearance since the merger, Mackovic was fired for what Hunt described as a lack of chemistry.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Frank_Gansz" title="Frank Gansz">Frank Gansz</a> served as head coach for the next two seasons, but won only eight of 31 games.<sup id="cite_ref-History_80s_25-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_80s-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marty_Schottenheimer_era">Marty Schottenheimer era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kansas_City_Chiefs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Marty Schottenheimer era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On December 19, 1988, owner Lamar Hunt hired <a href="/wiki/Carl_Peterson" title="Carl Peterson">Carl Peterson</a> as the team's new president, general manager, and chief executive officer. Peterson fired head coach Frank Gansz two weeks after taking over and hired <a href="/wiki/Marty_Schottenheimer" title="Marty Schottenheimer">Marty Schottenheimer</a> as the club's seventh head coach.<sup id="cite_ref-History_80s_25-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_80s-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/1988_NFL_Draft" title="1988 NFL Draft">1988</a> and <a href="/wiki/1989_NFL_Draft" title="1989 NFL Draft">1989</a> <a href="/wiki/NFL_Draft" class="mw-redirect" title="NFL Draft">NFL Drafts</a>, the Chiefs selected both defensive end <a href="/wiki/Neil_Smith_(American_football)" title="Neil Smith (American football)">Neil Smith</a> and linebacker <a href="/wiki/Derrick_Thomas" title="Derrick Thomas">Derrick Thomas</a>, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-History_80s_25-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_80s-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-History_90s_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_90s-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The defense that Thomas and Smith anchored in their seven seasons together was a big reason why the Chiefs reached the postseason in six straight years.<sup id="cite_ref-Althaus_63_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Althaus_63-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Schottenheimer's ten-season tenure as head coach, the Chiefs became a perennial playoff contender, featuring offensive players including <a href="/wiki/Steve_DeBerg" title="Steve DeBerg">Steve DeBerg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christian_Okoye" title="Christian Okoye">Christian Okoye</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephone_Paige" title="Stephone Paige">Stephone Paige</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barry_Word" title="Barry Word">Barry Word</a>, a strong defense, anchored by Thomas, Smith, Albert Lewis and Deron Cherry, and on special teams, <a href="/wiki/Nick_Lowery" title="Nick Lowery">Nick Lowery</a>, then the most accurate kicker in NFL History.<sup id="cite_ref-PFHOF_8-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFHOF-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The team recorded a 101–58–1 record, and clinched seven playoff berths.<sup id="cite_ref-Schottenheimer_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schottenheimer-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The Chiefs' 1993 season was the franchise's most successful in 22 years.<sup id="cite_ref-History_90s_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_90s-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> With newly acquired quarterback <a href="/wiki/Joe_Montana" title="Joe Montana">Joe Montana</a> and running back <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Allen" title="Marcus Allen">Marcus Allen</a>, two former <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">Super Bowl</a> champions and MVPs, the Chiefs further strengthened their position in the NFL.<sup id="cite_ref-History_90s_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_90s-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The 11–5 Chiefs defeated the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Steelers" title="Pittsburgh Steelers">Pittsburgh Steelers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Houston_Oilers" class="mw-redirect" title="Houston Oilers">Houston Oilers</a> on their way to the franchise's first <a href="/wiki/AFC_Championship_Game" title="AFC Championship Game">AFC Championship Game</a> appearance against the Buffalo Bills.<sup id="cite_ref-History_90s_30-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_90s-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The Chiefs were overwhelmed by the Bills and lost the game by a score of 30–13.<sup id="cite_ref-History_90s_30-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_90s-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The Chiefs' victory on January 16, 1994, against the Oilers remained the franchise's last post-season victory for 21 years until their 30–0 victory over the Houston Texans on January 9, 2016.
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/NFL_playoffs,_1995%E2%80%9396" class="mw-redirect" title="NFL playoffs, 1995–96">1995 NFL playoffs</a>, the 13–3 Chiefs hosted the <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis_Colts" title="Indianapolis Colts">Indianapolis Colts</a> in a cold, damp late afternoon game at Arrowhead Stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-PFR_13-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFR-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-History_90s_30-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_90s-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Kansas City lost the game 10–7 against the underdog Colts, after <a href="/wiki/Placekicker" title="Placekicker">kicker</a> <a href="/wiki/Lin_Elliot" class="mw-redirect" title="Lin Elliot">Lin Elliot</a> missed three field goal attempts and quarterback Steve Bono threw three interceptions.<sup id="cite_ref-History_90s_30-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_90s-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The Chiefs selected <a href="/wiki/Tight_end" title="Tight end">tight end</a> <a href="/wiki/Tony_Gonzalez" title="Tony Gonzalez">Tony Gonzalez</a> with the 13th overall selection in the <a href="/wiki/1997_NFL_Draft" title="1997 NFL Draft">1997 NFL Draft</a>, a move which some considered to be a gamble being that Gonzalez was primarily a <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> player at <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">California</a>. During a 1997 season full of injuries to starting quarterback <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Grbac" title="Elvis Grbac">Elvis Grbac</a>, backup quarterback <a href="/wiki/Rich_Gannon" title="Rich Gannon">Rich Gannon</a> took the reins of the Chiefs' offense as the team headed to another 13–3 season.<sup id="cite_ref-PFR_13-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFR-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-History_90s_30-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_90s-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Head coach Marty Schottenheimer chose Grbac to start the playoff game against the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Broncos" title="Denver Broncos">Denver Broncos</a> despite Gannon's successes in previous weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-History_90s_30-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_90s-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Grbac's production in the game was lacking, and the Chiefs lost to the Broncos 14–10.<sup id="cite_ref-History_90s_30-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_90s-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Denver went on to capture their fifth AFC Championship by defeating Pittsburgh, and then defeated the Green Bay Packers in <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXXII" title="Super Bowl XXXII">Super Bowl XXXII</a>. Coach Schottenheimer announced his resignation from the Chiefs following the 1998 season.
</p>
<h3><span id="1999.E2.80.932006"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1999–2006">1999–2006</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kansas_City_Chiefs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1999–2006">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following Schottenheimer's resignation, defensive coordinator <a href="/wiki/Gunther_Cunningham" title="Gunther Cunningham">Gunther Cunningham</a> took over coaching duties for the next two seasons, compiling a 16–16 record.<sup id="cite_ref-History_90s_30-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_90s-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> By the end of the Chiefs' decade of regular-season dominance, Gannon had signed with the Oakland Raiders, Neil Smith signed with the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Broncos" title="Denver Broncos">Denver Broncos</a>, and Derrick Thomas was paralyzed from a car accident on January 23, 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-History_90s_30-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_90s-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Thomas died from complications of his injury weeks later.<sup id="cite_ref-History_90s_30-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_90s-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> After allegedly reading online that he would be relieved of duties, head coach Gunther Cunningham was fired.<sup id="cite_ref-Chiefs_name_Gunther_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chiefs_name_Gunther-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tony_Gonzalez_at_2005_Pro_Bowl_050213-N-3019M-002.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Tony_Gonzalez_at_2005_Pro_Bowl_050213-N-3019M-002.jpg/200px-Tony_Gonzalez_at_2005_Pro_Bowl_050213-N-3019M-002.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="344" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Tony_Gonzalez_at_2005_Pro_Bowl_050213-N-3019M-002.jpg/300px-Tony_Gonzalez_at_2005_Pro_Bowl_050213-N-3019M-002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Tony_Gonzalez_at_2005_Pro_Bowl_050213-N-3019M-002.jpg/400px-Tony_Gonzalez_at_2005_Pro_Bowl_050213-N-3019M-002.jpg 2x" data-file-width="872" data-file-height="1500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tony_Gonzalez_at_2005_Pro_Bowl_050213-N-3019M-002.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tony_Gonzalez" title="Tony Gonzalez">Tony Gonzalez</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2005_Pro_Bowl" title="2005 Pro Bowl">2005 Pro Bowl</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Priest_Holmes_speaks_with_soldiers_CROPPED.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Priest_Holmes_speaks_with_soldiers_CROPPED.jpg/200px-Priest_Holmes_speaks_with_soldiers_CROPPED.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Priest_Holmes_speaks_with_soldiers_CROPPED.jpg/300px-Priest_Holmes_speaks_with_soldiers_CROPPED.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Priest_Holmes_speaks_with_soldiers_CROPPED.jpg/400px-Priest_Holmes_speaks_with_soldiers_CROPPED.jpg 2x" data-file-width="578" data-file-height="654" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Priest_Holmes_speaks_with_soldiers_CROPPED.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Priest_Holmes" title="Priest Holmes">Priest Holmes</a> became one of the league's top backs in the early 2000s</div></div></div>
<p>Looking to change the Chiefs' game plan which relied on a tough defensive strategy for the past decade, Carl Peterson contacted <a href="/wiki/Dick_Vermeil" title="Dick Vermeil">Dick Vermeil</a> about the Chiefs' head coaching vacancy for the 2001 season.<sup id="cite_ref-Chiefs_name_Gunther_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chiefs_name_Gunther-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Vermeil previously led the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Rams" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Louis Rams">St. Louis Rams</a> to a victory in <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXXIV" title="Super Bowl XXXIV">Super Bowl XXXIV</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Vermeil was hired on January 12. The Chiefs then traded a first-round draft pick in the <a href="/wiki/2001_NFL_Draft" title="2001 NFL Draft">2001 NFL Draft</a> to St. Louis for quarterback <a href="/wiki/Trent_Green" title="Trent Green">Trent Green</a> and signed free agent running back <a href="/wiki/Priest_Holmes" title="Priest Holmes">Priest Holmes</a> to be the team's cornerstones on offense.<sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2003, Kansas City began the season with nine consecutive victories, a franchise record.<sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> They finished the season with a 13–3 record and the team's offense led the NFL in several categories under the direction of USA Today's Offensive Coach of the Year honoree, Al Saunders.<sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Running back <a href="/wiki/Priest_Holmes" title="Priest Holmes">Priest Holmes</a> surpassed <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Faulk" title="Marshall Faulk">Marshall Faulk</a>'s single-season touchdown record by scoring his 27th rushing touchdown against the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Bears" title="Chicago Bears">Chicago Bears</a> in the team's regular season finale.<sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Althaus_65_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Althaus_65-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The team clinched the second seed in the <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_NFL_playoffs" title="2003–04 NFL playoffs">2004 NFL playoffs</a> and hosted the <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis_Colts" title="Indianapolis Colts">Indianapolis Colts</a> in the AFC Divisional Playoffs.<sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> In a game where neither team punted, the Chiefs lost the shoot-out 38–31.<sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> It was the third time in nine seasons that the Chiefs went 8–0 at home in the regular season, only to lose their post-season opener at Arrowhead.
</p><p>After a disappointing 7–9 record in 2004, the 2005 Chiefs finished with a 10–6 record but no playoff berth.<sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> They were the fourth team since 1990 to miss the playoffs with a 10–6 record.<sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Running back <a href="/wiki/Larry_Johnson_(running_back)" title="Larry Johnson (running back)">Larry Johnson</a> started in place of the injured Priest Holmes and rushed for 1,750 yards in only nine starts.<sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Prior to the Chiefs' final game of the season, head coach Dick Vermeil announced his retirement.<sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The Chiefs won the game 37–3 over the playoff-bound <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Bengals" title="Cincinnati Bengals">Cincinnati Bengals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Huard_and_Croyle.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Huard_and_Croyle.JPG/220px-Huard_and_Croyle.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="94" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Huard_and_Croyle.JPG/330px-Huard_and_Croyle.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Huard_and_Croyle.JPG/440px-Huard_and_Croyle.JPG 2x" data-file-width="981" data-file-height="421" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Huard_and_Croyle.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Damon_Huard" title="Damon Huard">Damon Huard</a> (left) and <a href="/wiki/Brodie_Croyle" title="Brodie Croyle">Brodie Croyle</a> (right) both served as the Chiefs' starting quarterback after <a href="/wiki/Trent_Green" title="Trent Green">Trent Green</a>'s departure</div></div></div>
<p>Within two weeks of Vermeil's resignation, the Chiefs returned to their defensive roots with the selection of its next head coach.<sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The team introduced <a href="/wiki/Herman_Edwards" class="mw-redirect" title="Herman Edwards">Herman Edwards</a>, a former Chiefs scout and head coach of the New York Jets, as the team's tenth head coach after trading a fourth-round selection in the <a href="/wiki/2006_NFL_Draft" title="2006 NFL Draft">2006 NFL Draft</a> to the Jets.<sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Quarterback Trent Green suffered a severe concussion in the team's season opener to the Cincinnati Bengals which left him out of play for eight weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Backup quarterback <a href="/wiki/Damon_Huard" title="Damon Huard">Damon Huard</a> took over in Green's absence and led the Chiefs to a 5–3 record.<sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kansas City was awarded a <a href="/wiki/NFL_on_Thanksgiving_Day" title="NFL on Thanksgiving Day">Thanksgiving Day game</a> against the Denver Broncos in response to owner Lamar Hunt's lobbying for a third Thanksgiving Day game.<sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The Chiefs defeated the Broncos 19–10 in the first Thanksgiving Day game in Kansas City since 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Hunt was hospitalized at the time of the game and died weeks later on December 13 due to complications with <a href="/wiki/Prostate_cancer" title="Prostate cancer">prostate cancer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Maske,_Mark_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maske,_Mark-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The Chiefs honored their owner for the remainder of the season, as did the rest of the league.<sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:061231Jaguars-Chiefs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/061231Jaguars-Chiefs.jpg/220px-061231Jaguars-Chiefs.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/061231Jaguars-Chiefs.jpg/330px-061231Jaguars-Chiefs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/061231Jaguars-Chiefs.jpg/440px-061231Jaguars-Chiefs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2576" data-file-height="1932" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:061231Jaguars-Chiefs.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>By defeating the <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Jaguars" title="Jacksonville Jaguars">Jaguars</a> on December 31, 2006, the Chiefs clinched a playoff berth after multiple other teams lost throughout the day</div></div></div>
<p>Trent Green returned in the middle of the season, but struggled in the final stretch,<sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> and running back Larry Johnson set an NFL record with 416 carries in a season.<sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Kansas City managed to clinch their first <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_NFL_playoffs" title="2006–07 NFL playoffs">playoff berth</a> in three seasons with a 9–7 record and a bizarre sequence of six losses from other AFC teams on New Year's Eve, culminating with a Broncos loss to the 49ers.<sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The Indianapolis Colts hosted the Chiefs in the Wild Card playoffs and defeated Kansas City 23–8.
</p>
<h3><span id="2007.E2.80.932012.2C_second_decline"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2007–2012,_second_decline">2007–2012, second decline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kansas_City_Chiefs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2007–2012, second decline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Larry_Johnson_Chiefs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7e/Larry_Johnson_Chiefs.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="256" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="150" data-file-height="256" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Larry_Johnson_Chiefs.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Larry_Johnson_(running_back)" title="Larry Johnson (running back)">Larry Johnson</a> in 2006</div></div></div>
<p>In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Trent_Green" title="Trent Green">Trent Green</a> was traded to the Miami Dolphins<sup id="cite_ref-Green_goes_to_Dolphins_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Green_goes_to_Dolphins-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> leaving the door open for either Damon Huard or <a href="/wiki/Brodie_Croyle" title="Brodie Croyle">Brodie Croyle</a> to become the new starting quarterback.<sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> After starting the season with a 4–3 record, the Chiefs lost the remaining nine games when running back Larry Johnson suffered a season-ending foot injury and the quarterback position lacked stability with Huard and Croyle.<sup id="cite_ref-History_2000s_34-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_2000s-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Despite the team's 4–12 record, tight end <a href="/wiki/Tony_Gonzalez" title="Tony Gonzalez">Tony Gonzalez</a> broke <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Sharpe" title="Shannon Sharpe">Shannon Sharpe</a>'s NFL record for touchdowns at the position (63) and <a href="/wiki/Defensive_end" title="Defensive end">defensive end</a> <a href="/wiki/Jared_Allen" title="Jared Allen">Jared Allen</a> led the NFL in <a href="/wiki/Quarterback_sacks" class="mw-redirect" title="Quarterback sacks">quarterback sacks</a> with 15.5.<sup id="cite_ref-PFR_13-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFR-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Chiefs began their 2008 season with the youngest team in the NFL.<sup id="cite_ref-Interesting_list_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Interesting_list-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The starting lineup had an average of 25.5 years of age.<sup id="cite_ref-Interesting_list_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Interesting_list-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> By releasing several veteran players such as cornerback <a href="/wiki/Ty_Law" title="Ty Law">Ty Law</a> and wide receiver <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Kennison" title="Eddie Kennison">Eddie Kennison</a> and trading defensive end Jared Allen,<sup id="cite_ref-KC_trades_DE_Jared_Allen_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KC_trades_DE_Jared_Allen-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> the Chiefs began a youth movement.<sup id="cite_ref-Interesting_list_37-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Interesting_list-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Thigpen_to_start_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thigpen_to_start-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The Chiefs had a league-high thirteen selections in the <a href="/wiki/2008_NFL_Draft" title="2008 NFL Draft">2008 NFL Draft</a> and chose defensive tackle <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Dorsey" title="Glenn Dorsey">Glenn Dorsey</a> and offensive lineman <a href="/wiki/Branden_Albert" title="Branden Albert">Branden Albert</a> in the first round. Analysts quickly called Kansas City's selections as the best of the entire draft.<sup id="cite_ref-KC_trades_DE_Jared_Allen_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KC_trades_DE_Jared_Allen-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Chiefs&#39;_Day_1_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chiefs&#39;_Day_1-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Draft_yields_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Draft_yields-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Several_&#39;08_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Several_&#39;08-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Entering the season, the Chiefs were unsure if injury-prone quarterback Brodie Croyle, who was the incumbent starter, could be their quarterback in the long-term.<sup id="cite_ref-Several_&#39;08_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Several_&#39;08-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Croyle was injured in the team's first game of the season and Damon Huard started in Croyle's absence.<sup id="cite_ref-Croyle_out_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Croyle_out-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tyler_Thigpen" title="Tyler Thigpen">Tyler Thigpen</a> become the third Chiefs starting quarterback in as many games for a start against the <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons" title="Atlanta Falcons">Atlanta Falcons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Falcons_back_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Falcons_back-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> After a poor performance by Thigpen, in which he threw three interceptions against the Falcons defense,<sup id="cite_ref-Falcons_back_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Falcons_back-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Huard was retained as the starting quarterback.<sup id="cite_ref-Huard_will_start_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Huard_will_start-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The Chiefs struggled off the field as much as on as tight end Tony Gonzalez demanded a trade and running back Larry Johnson was involved in legal trouble.<sup id="cite_ref-Johnson_under_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johnson_under-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-spitting_in_woman&#39;s_face_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spitting_in_woman&#39;s_face-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Chiefs_willing_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chiefs_willing-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Gonzalez_tells_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gonzalez_tells-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Croyle returned for the Chiefs' game against the Tennessee Titans, but both he and Damon Huard suffered season-ending injuries in the game.<sup id="cite_ref-Croyle_sprains_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Croyle_sprains-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The Chiefs reorganized their offense to a new <a href="/wiki/Spread_offense" title="Spread offense">spread offense</a> game plan focused around Tyler Thigpen.<sup id="cite_ref-Thigpen_to_start_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thigpen_to_start-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Breaking_the_Mold_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Breaking_the_Mold-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Spread_changes_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spread_changes-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The Chiefs' new offense was implemented to help Thigpen play to the best of his abilities and also following the absence of Larry Johnson, who was suspended for his off-field conduct.<sup id="cite_ref-spitting_in_woman&#39;s_face_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spitting_in_woman&#39;s_face-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Breaking_the_Mold_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Breaking_the_Mold-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Spread_changes_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spread_changes-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Johnson_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johnson-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The Chiefs made a huge gamble by using the spread offense, as most in the NFL believe that it cannot work in professional football, and also head coach Herman Edwards was traditionally in favor of more conservative, run-oriented game plans.<sup id="cite_ref-Spread_changes_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spread_changes-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alleman_Blocking.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Alleman_Blocking.jpg/220px-Alleman_Blocking.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Alleman_Blocking.jpg/330px-Alleman_Blocking.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Alleman_Blocking.jpg/440px-Alleman_Blocking.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4304" data-file-height="2852" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alleman_Blocking.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Chiefs hosting the <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_Bills" title="Buffalo Bills">Buffalo Bills</a> in 2009; Quarterback <a href="/wiki/Matt_Cassel" title="Matt Cassel">Matt Cassel</a>, wearing #7</div></div></div>
<p>The 2008 season ended with a franchise worst 2–14 record, where the team suffered historic blowout defeats nearly week-in and week-out.<sup id="cite_ref-PFR_13-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFR-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Falcons_back_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Falcons_back-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Titans_extend_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Titans_extend-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> a 34–0 shut-out to the <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Panthers" title="Carolina Panthers">Carolina Panthers</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Williams&#39;_career-best_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Williams&#39;_career-best-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> and allowed a franchise-high 54 points against the Buffalo Bills.<sup id="cite_ref-Edwards_helps_Bills_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Edwards_helps_Bills-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The team's general manager, chief executive officer, and team president Carl Peterson resigned at the end of the season,<sup id="cite_ref-Chiefs_GM_Peterson_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chiefs_GM_Peterson-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> and former <a href="/wiki/New_England_Patriots" title="New England Patriots">New England Patriots</a> vice president of player personnel <a href="/wiki/Scott_Pioli" title="Scott Pioli">Scott Pioli</a> was hired as his replacement for 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-Pioli_to_join_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pioli_to_join-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dwayne_Bowe.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Dwayne_Bowe.JPG/220px-Dwayne_Bowe.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="327" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Dwayne_Bowe.JPG/330px-Dwayne_Bowe.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Dwayne_Bowe.JPG/440px-Dwayne_Bowe.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1223" data-file-height="1817" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dwayne_Bowe.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dwayne_Bowe" title="Dwayne Bowe">Dwayne Bowe</a></div></div></div>
<p>On January 23, 2009, Herman Edwards was fired as head coach,<sup id="cite_ref-Chiefs_fire_Edwards_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chiefs_fire_Edwards-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Edwards_relieved_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Edwards_relieved-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> and two weeks later <a href="/wiki/Todd_Haley" title="Todd Haley">Todd Haley</a> signed a four-year contract to become Edwards' successor.<sup id="cite_ref-Haley_named_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haley_named-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Chiefs_hire_Cardinals_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chiefs_hire_Cardinals-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Haley had a background with Pioli, which made him an attractive hire for Pioli's first coach in Kansas City.
</p><p>In April 2009, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Gonzalez" title="Tony Gonzalez">Tony Gonzalez</a> was traded to the <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons" title="Atlanta Falcons">Atlanta Falcons</a> after failed trade attempts over the previous two seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-Chiefs_trade_Gonzalez_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chiefs_trade_Gonzalez-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Notably, head coach Todd Haley fired offensive coordinator <a href="/wiki/Chan_Gailey" title="Chan Gailey">Chan Gailey</a> just weeks before the start of the 2009 season and chose to take on the coordinator duties himself. Throughout 2009 the Chiefs acquired veterans to supplement the Chiefs' young talent including <a href="/wiki/Matt_Cassel" title="Matt Cassel">Matt Cassel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Vrabel" title="Mike Vrabel">Mike Vrabel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Engram" title="Bobby Engram">Bobby Engram</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Brown_(American_football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mike Brown (American football)">Mike Brown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Chambers" title="Chris Chambers">Chris Chambers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Andy_Alleman" title="Andy Alleman">Andy Alleman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Chiefs_complete_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chiefs_complete-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cassel,_Vrabel_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cassel,_Vrabel-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Chiefs_claim_Chambers_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chiefs_claim_Chambers-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The team finished with a 4–12 record, just a two-game improvement upon their record from the 2008 season.
</p><p>For the 2010 season, the Chiefs made significant hires for their coaching staff, bringing on former Patriots assistant coaches <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Weis" title="Charlie Weis">Charlie Weis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romeo_Crennel" title="Romeo Crennel">Romeo Crennel</a> to coach the offense and defense, respectively. The coaching additions proved to be very successful, as the Chiefs would go on to secure their first AFC West title since 2003. Their ten victories in the 2010 season combined for as many as the team had won in their previous three seasons combined.
</p><p>On January 9, 2011, the Chiefs lost their home Wild Card playoff game to the Baltimore Ravens 30–7. Six players were chosen for the Pro Bowl: Dwayne Bowe, <a href="/wiki/Jamaal_Charles" title="Jamaal Charles">Jamaal Charles</a>, Brian Waters, Tamba Hali, Matt Cassel, and rookie safety Eric Berry. Jamaal Charles won the FEDEX ground player of the year award and Dwayne Bowe led the NFL in Touchdown Receptions.
</p><p>For their first pick in the <a href="/wiki/2011_NFL_draft" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 NFL draft">2011 NFL draft</a>, and 26th overall, the team selected <a href="/wiki/Jon_Baldwin" title="Jon Baldwin">Jonathan Baldwin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wide_Receiver" class="mw-redirect" title="Wide Receiver">Wide Receiver</a> from <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Panthers_football" title="Pittsburgh Panthers football">Pitt</a>. After a poor start, Haley was relieved of duties as Head Coach on December 12. Clark Hunt made note of "bright spots at different points this season", but felt that overall the Chiefs were not progressing.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The highest point of the 2011 season was an upset win against the Packers, who at that time, were undefeated with a 13–0 record.
</p><p>The 2012 Chiefs became the first team since the 1929 <a href="/wiki/Buffalo_(1920s_NFL_teams)" class="mw-redirect" title="Buffalo (1920s NFL teams)">Buffalo Bisons</a> to not lead in regulation through any of their first nine games. The Chiefs tied their franchise worst record of 2–14 and clinched the No. 1 overall pick in the <a href="/wiki/2013_NFL_Draft" title="2013 NFL Draft">2013 NFL Draft</a>. It is the first time since the merger they have held the first overall pick.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Andy_Reid.2C_John_Dorsey_era"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Andy_Reid,_John_Dorsey_era">Andy Reid, John Dorsey era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kansas_City_Chiefs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Andy Reid, John Dorsey era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following the 2012 season, the Chiefs fired head coach <a href="/wiki/Romeo_Crennel" title="Romeo Crennel">Romeo Crennel</a> and general manager <a href="/wiki/Scott_Pioli" title="Scott Pioli">Scott Pioli</a>. Former <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Eagles" title="Philadelphia Eagles">Philadelphia Eagles</a> head coach <a href="/wiki/Andy_Reid" title="Andy Reid">Andy Reid</a> was brought in as head coach to work with new general manager <a href="/wiki/John_Dorsey_(American_football)" title="John Dorsey (American football)">John Dorsey</a>, a former <a href="/wiki/Green_Bay_Packers" title="Green Bay Packers">Green Bay Packers</a> head scout.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Andy_reid_2018_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Andy_reid_2018_%28cropped%29.jpg/175px-Andy_reid_2018_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="175" height="213" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Andy_reid_2018_%28cropped%29.jpg/263px-Andy_reid_2018_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Andy_reid_2018_%28cropped%29.jpg/350px-Andy_reid_2018_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1660" data-file-height="2017" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Andy_reid_2018_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Coach <a href="/wiki/Andy_Reid" title="Andy Reid">Andy Reid</a> in 2018</div></div></div>
<p>The Chiefs acquired quarterback <a href="/wiki/Alex_Smith" title="Alex Smith">Alex Smith</a> from the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_49ers" title="San Francisco 49ers">San Francisco 49ers</a> for the Chiefs' second-round pick, 34th overall, in the 2013 draft and a conditional pick in 2014 draft.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Matt Cassel was released shortly after. The Chiefs selected <a href="/wiki/Eric_Fisher_(American_football)" title="Eric Fisher (American football)">Eric Fisher</a> with the first overall pick of the <a href="/wiki/2013_NFL_Draft" title="2013 NFL Draft">2013 NFL Draft</a>.
</p><p>The Chiefs started 9–0 for the second time in team history. They would lead their wildcard game against the <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis_Colts" title="Indianapolis Colts">Indianapolis Colts</a> 38–10 shortly after halftime, but they would collapse late and lose, 45–44.
</p><p>In 2014, the Chiefs attempted to make the playoffs for the second straight season for the first time since 1995, however, they finished 9–7 and were eliminated in Week 17.
</p><p>After a promising win for the Chiefs against Houston in Week 1, Kansas City went on a five-game losing streak culminating in a 16–10 loss to Minnesota and the loss of Jamaal Charles to a torn ACL. However, they managed one of the most improbable season comebacks in the NFL and won ten straight to improve their record from 1–5 to 11–5. The team clinched a playoff berth after a 17–13 win over Cleveland in Week 16 to become only the second NFL team to do so after the merger.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (February 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The streak achieved by the Chiefs broke a franchise record for 9 straight (2003, 2013) and second 9 plus game win streak under Reid. After a Week 17 win over Oakland 23–17, the Chiefs achieved their longest winning streak in franchise history at ten games. They qualified for the playoffs, playing in the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_NFL_playoffs" title="2015–16 NFL playoffs">2015 AFC Wild-Card playoff game</a>, held at <a href="/wiki/NRG_Stadium" title="NRG Stadium">NRG Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Houston" title="Houston">Houston, Texas</a> on January 9, 2016. The Chiefs defeated the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Texans" title="Houston Texans">Houston Texans</a> 30–0 to earn their first <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League_playoffs" class="mw-redirect" title="National Football League playoffs">NFL playoff</a> win in 23 seasons, dating back to the <a href="/wiki/1993%E2%80%9394_NFL_playoffs" title="1993–94 NFL playoffs">1993–94 NFL playoffs</a>, a win that also came in Houston. The Chiefs' Wild-Card playoff victory ended what was at the time the third-longest <a href="/wiki/List_of_NFL_franchise_post-season_droughts" title="List of NFL franchise post-season droughts">drought</a> in the NFL, and it also ended a then NFL record eight-game playoff losing streak.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Riddled with injuries, they were defeated by the New England Patriots 27–20 in the AFC Divisional Round.
</p><p>After facing a 24–3 deficit with six minutes left in the 3rd quarter, the Chiefs engineered a 33–27 comeback win against the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Chargers" class="mw-redirect" title="San Diego Chargers">San Diego Chargers</a> ending with a two-yard touchdown run by Alex Smith in overtime to give the Chiefs their largest regular season comeback to start the season at 1–0.
</p><p>On <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League_Christmas_games" title="National Football League Christmas games">Christmas Day</a>, the Chiefs defeated the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Broncos" title="Denver Broncos">Denver Broncos</a> 33–10 to give Kansas City their tenth straight win against divisional opponents.
</p><p>On January 1, 2017, the Chiefs clinched the AFC West and the second seed going into the playoffs that year. They clinched the 2nd seed in the AFC but fell to the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Steelers" title="Pittsburgh Steelers">Pittsburgh Steelers</a> 18–16 as <a href="/wiki/Chris_Boswell" title="Chris Boswell">Chris Boswell</a> hit 6 field goals.
</p><p>The Chiefs finished the year with a 10–6 record, and won the AFC West. This was the first time in Chiefs history to win the AFC West in back to back years.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> In the Wild Card round the Chiefs lost a tight game to the <a href="/wiki/Tennessee_Titans" title="Tennessee Titans">Tennessee Titans</a> 22–21, allowing <a href="/wiki/Derrick_Henry" title="Derrick Henry">Derrick Henry</a> to rush for 156 yards. The loss extended their NFL record for most consecutive home playoff losses to six.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The game marked the end of Alex Smith's five-year tenure with the Chiefs, as he was traded to the Washington Redskins a few weeks later.
</p>
<h3><span id="Patrick_Mahomes_era.2C_second_Super_Bowl_win"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Patrick_Mahomes_era,_second_Super_Bowl_win">Patrick Mahomes era, second Super Bowl win</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kansas_City_Chiefs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Patrick Mahomes era, second Super Bowl win">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Patrick_Mahomes_II.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Patrick_Mahomes_II.JPG/220px-Patrick_Mahomes_II.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="295" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Patrick_Mahomes_II.JPG/330px-Patrick_Mahomes_II.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Patrick_Mahomes_II.JPG/440px-Patrick_Mahomes_II.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1796" data-file-height="2408" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Patrick_Mahomes_II.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Patrick Mahomes, the Chiefs starting quarterback since 2018</div></div></div>
<p>The Chiefs began the 2018 season with first-year starter <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Mahomes" title="Patrick Mahomes">Patrick Mahomes</a> as their quarterback and finished the regular season with a record of 12–4, clinching the AFC West for the third year in a row and the AFC's top seed. This included victories over division rivals <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Chargers" title="Los Angeles Chargers">Los Angeles Chargers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Raiders" class="mw-redirect" title="Oakland Raiders">Oakland Raiders</a> and <a href="/wiki/Denver_Broncos" title="Denver Broncos">Denver Broncos</a> (twice), along with important conference victories over the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Steelers" title="Pittsburgh Steelers">Pittsburgh Steelers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati_Bengals" title="Cincinnati Bengals">Cincinnati Bengals</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Jaguars" title="Jacksonville Jaguars">Jacksonville Jaguars</a>. Their first loss of the season came at the hands of the New England Patriots with a last-second field goal. In their second loss of the season against the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Rams" title="Los Angeles Rams">Los Angeles Rams</a> 51–54, the Kansas City Chiefs made history by becoming the first NFL team to lose a game after scoring more than 50 points. Mahomes finished the season with 5,097 yards and 50 touchdowns, both team records. He became the 11th quarterback to throw for 5,000 yards and the 3rd to throw for 50 touchdowns. He joined Peyton Manning as only the 2nd player in NFL history to throw for 5,000 yards and 50 touchdowns. For his performance during the season, he was named <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press_NFL_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="Associated Press NFL Most Valuable Player Award">AP NFL MVP</a>, the first Chief to win the award.
</p><p>In the AFC Divisional round on January 12, 2019, the Chiefs defeated the <a href="/wiki/Indianapolis_Colts" title="Indianapolis Colts">Indianapolis Colts</a> 31–13 to move on to the AFC Championship Game. This marked the Chiefs' first playoff win in Arrowhead Stadium in 25 years. This also enabled the Chiefs to host the AFC Championship Game for the first time ever. However, the following week, Kansas City's bid for its first Super Bowl berth in 49 years ended with a 31–37 overtime loss to the <a href="/wiki/New_England_Patriots" title="New England Patriots">New England Patriots</a>.
</p><p>The Chiefs finished the <a href="/wiki/2019_NFL_season" title="2019 NFL season">2019 regular season</a> with a 12–4 record, winning the <a href="/wiki/AFC_West" title="AFC West">AFC West</a> division title, and the AFC's second seed behind the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_Ravens" title="Baltimore Ravens">Baltimore Ravens</a>. The Chiefs defeated the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Texans" title="Houston Texans">Houston Texans</a> 51–31 in the AFC Divisional Game after falling behind 24–0 at the start of the second quarter with Mahomes throwing for five touchdowns. The Chiefs hosted their second AFC Championship game in consecutive years facing the sixth-seed <a href="/wiki/Tennessee_Titans" title="Tennessee Titans">Tennessee Titans</a>. The Chiefs then defeated the Titans 35–24 and advanced to <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_LIV" title="Super Bowl LIV">Super Bowl LIV</a>. This marked their first appearance in a Super Bowl since <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_IV" title="Super Bowl IV">Super Bowl IV</a>, 50 years earlier. 
</p><p>On February 2, 2020, in <a href="/wiki/Hard_Rock_Stadium" title="Hard Rock Stadium">Hard Rock Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Miami_Gardens" class="mw-redirect" title="Miami Gardens">Miami Gardens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>, the Chiefs played <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_LIV" title="Super Bowl LIV">Super Bowl LIV</a>, against the NFC top seed, the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_49ers" title="San Francisco 49ers">San Francisco 49ers</a>. With the game tied at 10 points each at halftime, Mahomes threw 2 interceptions in the 3rd quarter, which enabled the 49ers to take a 20–10 lead to the fourth quarter. However, the Chiefs advanced down field, and Mahomes rebounded big-time, throwing 2 touchdowns, to <a href="/wiki/Travis_Kelce" title="Travis Kelce">Travis Kelce</a> and <a href="/wiki/Damien_Williams" title="Damien Williams">Damien Williams</a>, respectively. With a 24–20 lead with under three minutes remaining, Williams had his second touchdown of the night, a 38-yard run, and the Chiefs lead 31–20. The game was sealed with a <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Garoppolo" title="Jimmy Garoppolo">Jimmy Garoppolo</a> interception with under a minute remaining. This marked the first time in NFL post-season history that a team faced 10 point deficits in 3 straight games, and won all 3 by 10 or more points. Patrick Mahomes won the <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="Super Bowl Most Valuable Player Award">Super Bowl Most Valuable Player Award</a>. This was the teams' first championship since 1969, and their first since the <a href="/wiki/AFL-NFL_Merger" class="mw-redirect" title="AFL-NFL Merger">AFL-NFL Merger</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Championships">Championships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kansas_City_Chiefs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Championships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Chiefs have won a total of three combined Super Bowl Championships and pre-Super Bowl AFL Championships, two were won as the Kansas City Chiefs, the other was under their original name, the Dallas Texans.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="American_Football_Conference_Championships">American Football Conference Championships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Kansas_City_Chiefs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: American Football Conference Championships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
